fa JTirsf Ssau% 1891.
attempt to supply a Directory, which may satisfy the
A. want of those persons interested in the names, addresses,
educational status, past and present appointments of the Clergy,
as well as the number of Church buildings, stipend, patronage,
and other useful particulars of the parishes in Australia and
Tasmania, was made owing to my time for some months being
only partly occupied by parochial duties, and the desire to render
this service to the Church. I hope the Directory may prove to
be of some use for reference by the Clergy, Patrons, Church-
wardens and others who may require the information now set
forth.
Some particulars of Diocesan Institutions, &c., have been
added in this issue, but when a second issue is called for, I hope
to enlarge the usefulness of the Directory by the addition of other
general matter of interest to Churchmen. Much of the additional
matter has already been prepared, but I have thought it better
not to increase the cost of printing, and consequently the price to
purchasers of copies of the Directory, for the first issue.
The matter recorded is as complete as my opportunities and
circumstances of a first compilation permitted, and I hope, with
the kind help of patrons, as the publication grows older, the
information will become as reliable and approach as near
completeness as the ever changing nature of its contents will
allow.
I shall be grateful if the Clergy will forward me as early as
they conveniently may all or any of the items enumerated on the
“ Particulars of Clergymen,” and “ Particulars of Parishes,” to be
found elsewhere in the Directory. (See coloured leaf pages 87 & 88).
Should errors have occurred, or alterations become requisite
in the particulars given in this issue of the Directory, I trust to
be informed of them, so that they may be rectified in the second
issue.
Aug. 1891. THE EDITOR.

LIVERPOOL, N.S.W.
Council:
THE MOST REV. THE PRIMATE
The Very Rev. the Dean of Sydney, I Trustees of the estate of the
The Hon. Edward Knox, ) late Thomas Moore
The Rev. C. F. D. Priddle
T, W. Taylor, Esq. | T. L. Peate, Esq.
HE MOORE COLLEGE GRAMMAR SCHOOL was founded in
1889, and since then there has been steady progress. The buildings,
formerly used as a Church of England Theological Training
College, consist of the Broughton Chapel, class-rooms and dormitories,
which, with the head-master’s house form the school quadrangle. No more
than two boys will be put in each of the dormitories, which are roomy
and lofty.
Attached to the School are six acres of playground ; and a few chains
away is the George’s River, which is admirably adapted for boating. A
Rowing Club is now being formed. Games and manly exercises are looked
upon as an essential part of the school discipline. In addition to Football
and Cricket Clubs, there is a Lawn Tennis Club, with sufficient ground for
several more courts. Boarders are encouraged to fill up spare time with
Natural History, Sketching, Photography, Fretwork, &c.
The Course o Study is arranged on the lines of the Junior, Senior and
Matriculation Examinations ; but boys are not encouraged to look upon
examinations as the sole end of education. The work is divided into
classical and modern sides—and a Preparatory School is established for
small boys.
Religious Instruction, according to the principles of the Church of
England, is part of the regular work. It is hoped that a School Chaplain
will soon be appointed.
Tuition (Grammar School) ... 3 guineas per quarter
~ (Preparatory School) ... 2 ~ ~ ~
Reduction will be made in the case of brothers and sons of the Clergy.
R. F. Irvine, Esq., M.A., and Senior Scholar, N.Z. ; for several
years a Master at Christ’s College, N.Z.
Mathematics ani) :
W. Stoddart, Esq., Peel Exhibitioner, Trinity College, Dublin.

The Bank has Branches in all the principal Cities and Towns in New
South Wales, Victoria, New Zealand, Queensland, South Australia
and Western Australia; and Agents in the following places :
Tasmania —The Commercial Bank of Tasmania, Ltd.
BEYOND THE COLONIES.
Scotland— The Royal Bank of Scotland. Ireland —The National Bank.
Liverpool—The North and South Wales Bank. Manchester —The Man-
chester and Liverpool District Bank. Birmingham —Lloyd’s Bank, Ltd.
Bristol and West of England —Stuckey’s Banking Company. Hamburg —
Messrs. H. J. Merck & Co. New York— The Bank of British North
America. San Francisco— The London and San Francisco Bank. Manilla
—Messrs. Kerr & Co. India. China, Ceylon, Mauritius, Singapore and
Batavia— The Chartered Mercantile Bank of India, London, and China,
and the Chartered Bank of India, Australia, and China. Rio Janeiro
The English Bank of Rio Janeiro. Africa— Standard Bank of South
Africa, Limited.
The Bank allows interest on Deposits, if lodged at periods, at rates
which may be ascertained at its various offices.
Collects for its customers dividends on shares in public companies, and
interest on debentures. Invests money on their behalf in Colonial
securities, or those of Great Britain.
Issues Drafts and Letters of Credit, and negotiates approved bills
payable at any of the above-named places ; and undertakes the agency of
other banks on such terms as may be agreed upon.

THE continued success of the Clergy Widows’ and Orphans’ Fund as a
benefit for the many, and not for the few, depends necessarily on these
two conditions :
First —The reception of an Annual Offertory from every Parish, in
addition to the Parochial Subscription.
Secondly —Larger and more liberal donations and subscriptions on the
part of Lay Members of the Church throughout the Diocese.
Should these conditions be complied with, the scale of Pensions might
be considerably increased. A very great accession to the Funds of the
Society would thus be secured, and a far wider and more general interest
aroused among Churchmen as to the operations and benefits of this excellent
institution, whose financial soundness has been more than once determined
by competent actuarial investigation.
Subscriptions and Donations may be sent direct to credit of
the Fund with the Bank of New South Wales, Sydney, N.S.W.

The Association was formed to uphold the Principles of the Church of
England, Protestant and Reformed ; to protest against encroachments
against her Doctrine and Established Ritual, and to discountenance
in every legitimate way Unauthorized Innovations.
The official organ of the Association is The Church of England
Intelligencer, published monthly.

ALLEN PASTORAL AID FUND.—Dio. of Adel. Consists of
the income derived from a sum given by the late Capt. W. Allen and
devoted to aid par. and mis. districts which are not end. ; Capital £6,986 ;
Income from interest £433.
ASSESSMENTS: MANAGEMENT EXPENSES-
Dio. of Adel. Made to meet working expenses, which includes
office management £2o'), printing &c. £BB, and about £3l for other require-
ments. Interest on the Harford Bequest provides about £29 a year, and
the Synodal Assessment on all the Chs. of the dio. is intended to defray
the expenses mentioned above. The assessment varies from £l3 Bs. 2d. to
to £1 55., and is levied according to the amount and sources of revenue.
If unpaid, it is deducted from the Grant-in-Aid (if any) alloted to the
Par. concerned.
Dio. of Ball. Income from Fees and Commissions £144, Marriage
Licenses £545. The items of expenditure include Assembly expenses,
salaries of officials, printing, rent, &c. It is a Fund for providing for the
expenses necessarily incurred in administering the affairs of the Ch.

Dio. of Goulb. Is made to pay the expenses of Diocesan, Provincial,
and General Synods. Parishes are divided into Five Sections, and assessed
from £5 to £1 each.
Dio. of Graft, and Armid. Assessments received (1890), £l4.
Printing and other expenses incurred £33.
Dio. of Perth. Levied to meet expenses of Synod, and range from
£l2 down to £2 Bs. for each parish. They amount to about £6B.
Dio. of Syd. Par. contribution for expenses of Synod and Registry
is levied on par. according to their estimated importance and revenue.
There are eleven Classes, named A. to K., the highest class (A.) being
assessed at £34 10s., and the lowest class (K.) at £2 a year.
BISHOPRIC END. FUND.—Dio. of Ball. Capital £20,408;
income from interest £1,546 ; Expenditure stip. £1,446; Commission £3B.
Bp’s. Fund. Dio. of Melb. Income from subscriptions, Ch. collections,
&c., about £7,000, interest from End. about £l,OOO. The fund serves to
increase the stipends of the parochial clergy.
BISHOP’S RENT FUND.—Dio. of Graft, and Armid. Collection
£lO.
CATHEDRAL BUILDING FUND.-Dio. of Adel. £lB,OOO
has been expended, £lO,OOO is available for building, and £22,000 will

Dio. of Tas. Capital invested £2,798.
CENTENNIAL FUND, dio. of Syd., was a thank offering for
success and prosperity, originated to mark the 100th year from the founda-
tion of the colony of N.S.W. ; capital abt. £19,000. The objects stated
are: (1) help to clergy in new districts, (2) extension of the episcopate,
(3) extension of missions, (4) grants on loans for Ch. building, (6) loans free
of interest to pay existing Ch. debts. Amount received £25,257, total
a mount contributed (promised) £41,465.
CHURCH BUILDINGS LOAN FUND.-Dio. of Syd.
Capital abt. £lO,OOO, originated in 1879t0 commemorate the 25thyearof Bp’s
Barker’s episcopate, to encourage and assist the payment of debts on
Ch. buildings, and to promote the erection, enlargement, or improvement
of Chs., Parsges, and Sch. hos. in the dio. Loans are granted free of
interest in sums of £5O to £l,OOO for any period up to 10 years, repayable
quarterly or half-yearly. Interest at the rate of ten per cent, per annum.
is made on all overdue instalments.
CH. END. FUND.—Dio. of Syd. Originated 1860 for End. in
land for the Ch. of the dio. of Syd. The original capital, inclusive of
accumulations of interest and further subscriptions, is invested in Aust.
Governmental securities, or lent in aid of Ch. work in the dio. in sums not
exceeding £5OO, for a period of not more than five years, the principal and
interest to be repaid in regular quarterly, half-yearly, or yearly instalments.
The capital of the fund is about £5,000.
CHURCH SOCIETY.—Dio. of Goulb. Aids a clergy sustentation
fund ; obtains clergy for unsupplied districts; procures End. for Chs. ; aids
in erecting, repairing, and enlarging Chs., Parsges, &c. ; assists in supporting
catechists ; circulates Bibles, Prayer Books, &c., through the Diocesan
Depot, and forms lending libraries ; establishes and encourages mis. to the
aborigines or other heathens ; and encourages the establishment of Ch. Schs.,
&c. Income: General £l,lBl, stipend £2,306, special £609.
CHURCH SOCIETY. —Dio. of Syd. Income for general purposes
about £5,000, total income about £23,000. The Society supplements the
stip. of clergy and the salaries of catechists in poor par.; in some instances
pays passage money or travelling expenses of clergy or catechists ; makes
grants : (1) to mis., (2) to encourage building of Chs., Parsges, or Sch. halls,
(3) to help to keep Ch. buildings in repair, and (4) to help poor parishes to
discharge diocesan pecuniary obligations. It has a Pension Fund for aged
clergy, and holds endowments for some parishes. The Society also receives
127
CHURCH DIRECTORY, 1891.


from the parishes the stipends due, and forwards the same to the clergy
concerned, or pays the amount to their Sydney Bankers.
CLERGY END. FUND.—Dio. of Ball. Is available solely for
grants towards the stip. of clergy. Capital £15,799 ; receipts from interest
£1,104.
CUSACK-RUSSELL SCHOLARSHIP.— Dio. of Ball.
Capital £1,260. Receipts from interest £3B. This Scholarship is open to
Readers who are candidates for Holy Orders.
DEAN AND CHAPTER.—Dio. of Adel. Incorporated ; have
income from interest on loans amounting to £3,865, and rents on freeholds
value £2,669 ; income and expenditure about £5OO a year, of which latter
£455 is for stip.
ENDOWMENT SOC.—Dio. of Adel., contributes three-fifths of a
sum for end., if two-fifths are raised in other ways by the congregation
concerned. When the sum for end. reaches £5OO current rate of interest
is paid, plus 15 per cent, on the amount of interest during the first five
years. Instalments of not less than £5 paid towards end. have 10 per cent,
interest paid on them. The system is planned to end. Chs. to the extent
of £lOO a year. When the capital end. exceeds £5OO, then for every £1
above £3O of annual income a seat in the Ch. must be set apart as free for
ever. The income derived is for the exclusive benefit of the clergyman,
and in case of a vacancy of the cure, the accruing income is disposed of by
the Standing Committee to pay a clergyman temporarily appointed, for the
general benefit of the cure, or for general end. purposes. £15,061 has been
contributed by the Society since its foundation in 1860 to 51 Chs. The
present capital is £12,760, and income £534.
GENERAL SUSTENTATION AND END. FUND-
Dio. of Perth ; capital £6,615.
GRANTS-IN-AID TO CLERICAL INCOMES.—Dio. of Adel.
Made to help young par. for a term of fifteen years. When the par. raises
£lOO a year for stip. £35 is added as a Grant-in-Aid, but no clergyman
receives more than £5O a year from the fund. If there is only a fortnightly
service held in the Ch. then the Grant-in-Aid is half the amount of that
allotted to a Ch. where a service is conducted each Sunday. The clergy
of end. Chs. receive no Grants-in-Aid, but if they also serve unend. Chs.
they receive Grants-in-Aid for the latter. Deductions from the amount of
Grant-in-Aid is made to clergy of partly end. Chs., and to clergy engaged
in tuition.
HARFORD BEQUEST. —Dio. of Adel. A bequest by Mr. Harford
realizes about £29, and is devoted to the expenses of Synod.
HOME MISSION FUND.—Dio. of Adel. ; the Par. Collections
are paid over to the appointed receiver before any alloted Grants-in-Aid
are paid to the several par. The Capital Loan Fund is £3,005. Loans to
Mis. Chs. amount to £2,576. Income from interest, Leigh Estate, Donations,
Collections, &c., about £2,674.
HOME MIS. PENNY ASSO.—Dio. of Adel., has five branches, and
its purpose is to raise money for the Bps. Home Mis. Income about £202.
Weekly subscriptions of one penny are collected.
HOME MIS. SOC.—Dio. of Adel. Formed 1883, consists of
subscribers of £1 Is. a year, and governed by an executive committee. Its
objects are (1) to supply clergy in new centres of pop. and in poor localities.
(2) To procure sites for Ch. buildings and aid by grant or loan, the erection
of Ch. buildings. (3) To provide additional curates in populous parishes.
Sums not exceeding £2OO (as a rule), are lent to be repaid with interest
within five years. Capital estimated to April 1892 at £3,005. Income
from subscriptions, &c. about £531.
INCORPORATED END. FUND.—Dio. of Adel. Capital £12,000,
with an income of £331. The Fund promotes the end. of par. to the
extent of £3O a year, and pays passage money of clergy to the colony ;
51 Chs. have been fully or partly end. by the Fund.

LEIQ-H ESTATE. —Dio. of Adel. A valuable property in the city
of Adel., yielding an income of £3,600, vested in the S.P.G. by Mr. Leigh
to promote Ch. work in S. A. Grants are made to the Bps. Home Mis.,

LOAN BUILDING FUND- —Dio. of Goulb. Is formed from
the surplus revenue of the Church Society. Loans are granted without
interest for a term of five years or more.
LOCAL END. FUND. —Dio. of Perth. The accruing income is
added to the Capital Account, except in the cases of Geralton and Beverley,
where, under special circumstances, it has been applied to the Rector’s
Stip.

—Dio. of Perth ; capital belonging to 18 different Chs. £5,399.

SCHOOL BOARD FUND- —Dio. of Ball. Income from

SUPERANNUATIONS, ANNUITIES, AND PENSIONS.—
Dio. of Adel, (founded 1877). Capital £5,765. The Clergy subscription
is £2 2s a year ; no medical certificate of health required ; 10 years’
membership required to entitle to an annuity ; no further subscription
required after 40 years’ membership ; all Clergy required to join, unless
specially exempted by the Bp. ; one-half of accumulated subscriptions
returned to Clergy on resigning Bps. license ; annuitants may do occasional
clerical duty ; the amount of annuity is calculated by length of service in
the dio. Income, £551 ; expenditure, £56. There are 34 subscribing
Clergy.
Dio. of Ball. Captial £4066. Income from Clergy subscriptions £144,
lay contributions £59, Ch. collections £lB9, interest £258.
Dio. of Melb. Capital £5930.
Dio. of Syd. (established 1876). The capital (now about £12,000)
is raised by a subscription of £5 year from a clergyman to constitute
him a claimant on the fund ; a payment of £8 a year by
the parish of such clergyman ; and by legacies, donations &c. Super-
annuated Clergy are entitled to the following pensions, viz. ;—A
claimant of 10 years membership, £75 a year ; 15 years £3O ; 20
years, £105; 25 years, £125; 30 years, £145; 35 years £165; 40
years, £185; 45 years, £205 a year. All Clergy are required to join the
fund on presentation to a Cure. There are 45 members of the fund, and
only one claimant.
Dio. of Syd. Pension Fund in connection with the Ch. Society,
Capital £3883. The Bp. nominates Clergy to be benefited by the fund,
the maximum allowance being £75 a year.
Dio of Tas. Capital £555. Income from Ch. collections £22, clergy
subscriptions £3, interest £24, expended for Sec. salary £l2.
SUSTENTATION AND CH. EXTENSION FUND.-Dio. of
Ball. Capital £20,283; income from subscriptions (capital a/c) £332,
interest £BB7, Ch. collections £305; subscriptions (current account) £7OB,
C. &C. Ch. Society £lOO. The capital is available as loans on easy terms
to erect Chs., schs., and parsges. The current income is spent chiefly in
grants to the stip. of clergy in poor and new districts.
WIDOWS & ORPHANS OF CLERGY FUND.-Dio.
of Adel, (founded in 1864). Capital £12083. Income £906, expenditure £493.
There are seven annuitants on the fund, the annuity being £55, with the
prospect of further increase. The subscription is—from married clergy
£4, from unmarried clergy £2. 34 clergy are subscribers to the fund.
129
CHURCH DIRECTORY, 1891.


Clergy resigning the Bps. license are entitled to half the amount paid by
them, and if subscribers for 15 years leave the diocese they are entitled to
continue membership.
Dio. of Goulb, Income is derived by :— {a) An annual collection in
every Ch. or Chapel where Divine service is conducted at least twice a
month ; (6) the annual payment of £6 by each parish in addition to a
collection ; (c) the annual payment of £6 by each licensed clergyman ; (t/)
interest accruing from capital ; (r) donations, subscriptions, and legacies.
Clergy are exempted from payment who cannot effect a Policy of
Assurance, and such as are assured for not less than £SOO are not required
to contribute. Members of the Fund may assure up to £IOOO in an
approved Insurance Soc., at Table A. rates of the A.M.P.S. The
Board appointed to manage the Fund undertakes the payment of approved
premiums.
Dio, of Graft, and Armid. Income; from clergy subscriptions £lO4,
from parishes £97, collections £96, and interest on Bank deposit.
Premiums are paid to the A.M.P.S. for six subscribing members £139,
and grants in aid of policies to nine others £lB2.
Dio. of Melb. and Ball. Capital £23,168. Collections £BS, lay sub-
scriptions £64. Pensions and allowances £ll9 to four recipients.
Dio. of Perth. Capital £402, income from interest £l9, subscriptions
£l6, offertories £ll. There are three subscribing clergy. Expenditure :
A.M. P. Soc. on policies £34.
Dio. of Syd. Capital about £17,000. Clergy subscribe £5 a year,
and another £5 is sought from the parish of the subscribing clergy-
man. Widows who have a claim on the Fund are entitled to a pension
according to the number of annual payments made by the deceased
clergyman and parish. Thus the pension resulting from five years’ sub-
scriptions is £3O a year to the widow, and £8 additional for each child
under 16 years old ; ten years’ subscriptions entitles to an annuity of £35,
and £8 for each child under 16 years old, with £2 added to the widow’s
allowance for 10 years, on each year’s subscriptions paid after 10 years.
If there has been no parochial subscriptions to the fund, the clergyman's
subscription entitles the widow to a pension of £25 a year, with £5
a year additional for each child under 16 years of age.
Dio. of Tas. Capital (1890) £3061. Income: interest £149, Ch.
Collections £6B, contributions £BS. Expenditure ; Aids to insurance £2l,
annuiries £SO, other charges £47.
Butcjtses.
ADELAIDE.—Founded 1847. Comprises the colony of South
Australia ; area 300,000 square miles, with the Bp’s, temporary oversight
of the Northern Territory since 1864. The Diocesan Synod was organised
in 1856. There are 63 licensed Clergy, 3 Archd., 10 Can., 10 Rural Deans,
43 parishes, 20 mission districts, and 137 Chs. and mission buildings. Ch.
pop. 76,000. The Bp’s, maximum stipend is £1,200, but the present stipend
only £950. Surplus income to be applied (1) to the formation of new
Bishoprics out of the dio. of Adel.; (2) to provide for retiring allowances
for the Bp's.; (3) to augment the Bp’s. Stipends.
BALLARAT.—Created out of Melb. dio. 30th Oct. 1873. The
eastern boundary is (roughly) the 144th meridian ; the other boundaries
are those of the colony of Victoria. ‘ Ch. pop. about 80,000 ; area 44,000
square miles. Income of Bp. £1,446. There are 55 clergy of the dio.
BATHURST.—The Bp’s, income is £BOO. There are 43 clergy of
the dio.
BRISBANE, consists of Queensland South of 22nd parallel of
latitude ; pop. of dio. 320,000 ; area 413,000 square miles ; clergy 63 ; Bp’s
income £l.OOO.

OOULBURN comprises the S.E. portion of N.S.W. There are 40
clergy of the dio. The Bp’s, income is derived from the interest on £16,000,
and State Aid £lOO.
GRAFTON AND ARMIDALE comprises that portion of N.S.W.
included between a line running W. from Camden Hewen to Liverpool
Ranges, thence to Walgett, and so due N. to S. boundary of Queensland.
Bp’s, income £580; area 75,000 square miles ; 27 clergy.
MELANESIA consists of the Melanesian Archipelago, and has an
area of 1,500 miles. There are 14 clergy, and the Bp’s, income is £5OO.
MELBOURNE consists of the Eastern half of the colony of Victoria.
The Bp’s, income is £2,000. Area 45,000 square miles. There are 162
clergy of the dio.
NEWCASTLE has 43 clergy ; its extent 70,000 square miles.
NORTHERN TERRITORY, under supervision of dio. of Adel.
The Bp. of Adel., in conjunction with the Bp. of Perth, have a scheme
before the S.P.G. in London, by which the grant at present set aside by
that society for the support of a clergyman in the Northern Territory
should be devoted by them towards the support of a Missionary Bishop,
who should endeavour to establish Ch. work in the North and North-West
of Australia.
NORTH QUEENSLAND consists of the portion of Queensland, N.
of the 22nd parallel of latitude.
PERTH. Capital invested £8,605 ; Local Income from interest £175,
rents £307, expenditure to Bp. £4lO, expenses £66. The See is provided
with a residence and grounds in the city of Perth. Bp’s, income £7OO.
The dio. consists of the colony of W.A. ; Ch. pop. 16,263—54 - 74 per cent,
of pop. of the colony. There are 74 Chs., and 25 clergy.
RIVERINA consists of theS.W. portion of N.S.W. There are 14
clergy of the dio. Bp’s, income is derived from the interest on £15,000.
There are 14 clergy.
SYDNEY, area 4,000 square miles. There are 100 parishes, 180Chs.
and other licensed buildings ; 155 clergy of the diocese ; Bp’s income from
End. abt. £3,500.
TASMANIA includes the whole colony. Bp’s, income from Local
Fund £l,OOO, and from Colonial Bishoprics Fund £409. Ch. pop. 76,098.
There are 51 clergy, 44 parishes, 150 Ohs. and other buildings used for
Divine Service, with 17,000 sit.; 73 consecrated Chs., of which 20 are free
and open ; 4,750 S. S. scholars, with 490 teachers.

COLLEGES
COLLEGIATE SCHOOL OF S. PETER, dio. of Adel., has accom-
modation for six Theo. Students.
MOORE COLL. dio. of Syd. Founded 1856 at Liverpool (N.S. W.),
now at Sydney. 150 clergymen have been ordained from this College
since its foundation.
S. BARNABAS’ COLL., dio. of Adel. The present built portion
provides two rooms each for six students, and serves candidates for
Holy Orders. The Theo. Tutorship is endowed with £5O a year.
S. PAUL’S COLL., dio. of Syd., is incorporated with Syd. Univ. by
Act of N.S. W. Parliament. Students must attend University Lectures
There are seven scholarships (five of which are for students intending
to take Holy Orders), and several divinity prizes given. Warden’s
Stip. £5OO, other sources £250, total £750 ; Vice-Warden’s £250 ; Tutor’s
£lOO ; Accountant’s £2O.
TRINITY COLL., dio. of Melb., was opened in 1872, has 15 endowed
scholarships; other scholarships of the value of £5O and upwards
each, are given by the Warden for competition, regardless of age,
sex, religion, or future profession. The lectures are open to non-
resident as well as resident students.
DEACONS, dio. of Adel., are ineligible for Incumbencies, and may
not leave the cure to which ordained without permission of the Bp.;
Deacons of other Dioceses will not be received by Bp. unless upon inquiry
satisfactory reasons exist for their leaving the dio. of ordination ; Deacons
licensed by the Bp. sit in Synod, may join in discussion, but have no
voting privilege.
Dio. of Ball. Candidates should apply to the Bp. six months
before time fixed for Ordination, and should hold certificate in
Theology of some one of the English and Irish Universities ; Trinity
Coll., Melbourne ; Moore Coll., N.S.W.; or of any other Theological Coll,
approved by the Bp. (S. Bees’ Coll., Cumberland is not so approved).
Candidates are required to undergo an examination in the Scriptures,
Prayer Book, Ch. Doctrine, Greek, Sermon Composition, Ch. History and
Pastoral Theology. Two further examinations, at six months’ interval,
are required before ordination to the Priesthood. Ordinations are held
at Christmas and Trinity.
DIOCESAN SCHOOLS
BLANDFORD SCH., dio. of Graft, and Armid., has a site of 10 acres
in Armid. The old property at Blandford has been sold.
CHURCH OF ENGLAND GRAMMAR SCHOOL, dio. of Melb., has
17 Masters or Professors, and 330 pupils.
COLLEGIATE SCHOOL OF S. PETER, dio. of Adel. Founded
1847 ;40 acres of land are attached to the school. There are 20 scholar-

is 108.
GEELONG GRAMMAR SCHOOL, dio. of Melb., has 7 Masters and
77 pupils.
KING’S SCH., PARRAMATTA, dio. of Syd. Founded and opened
1832. The school has seven acres of recreation grounds, a hospital, and a
Chapel.
MOORE COLL. GRAMMAR SCHOOL, LIVERPOOL, dio. of Syd.,
comprises the buildings which formerly served for Moore Theological 'Coll.
(See advt. p, 8.)
_ S. CATHERINE’S SCH., WAVERLEY, dio. of Syd. Founded
1856. Daughters of clergy receive board, residence, and education at about
one-third the fees paid by other pupils. The school has three and a half
acres of land attached. There is a Scholarship open to daughters of
clergy of Syd. dio. There are also some money prizes given.
S. PETER’S LADIES’COLL., ARMID ALE, dio. of Graft, and Armid.
SYDNEY. C. OF E. GRAMMAR SCH., North Syd., has 120

amount to £lBO2. (See Advt., p. 137 )

HOODS OF CLERGY denote the Degree conferred by a University
or College. The following are worn in Australia :
B.A. —Black hood trimmed with white Jur denotes B.A. of Sydney,
Oxford, Cambridge, Durham, Dublin, or Queens. (Irel.).
Black silk hood lined with dark blue silk denotes B.A. of Melbourne.
Black stuff hood edged with white silk denotes B.A. of Adelaide.
B.D. —Black silk nood lined with black silk denotes B.D. of Oxford,
Cambridge, Durham, or Dublin.
Black silk hood lined with violet silk denotes B.D. of Toronto.
MIIS. B. —Black silk hood trimmed with white fur denotes Mus. B. of
Dublin,
LL.B. and M.B , —Blue silk hood lined with white fur denotes LL.B.
or M.B. of Sydney.
Black silk hood lined with while fur denotes LL.B. of Melbourne.
Black silk hood edged with Napoleon blue silk denotes LL.B. of
Adelaide.
Black silk hood lined with white silk denotes LL. B. of Dublin.
M- A- —Black silk hood lined with light blue silk denotes M.A. of
Sydney.
Black silk hood lined with violet purple silk denotes M.A. of Melbourne.
Black silk hood lined ivith white silk and edged with white on the outer
fold denotes M.A. of Adelaide.
Black silk hood lined with white silk denotes M.A. of Cambridge or
Edinburgh.
Black silk hood lined with crimson silk denotes M.A. of Oxford.
Black silk hood lined with palatinate-purple silk denotes M.A. of
Durham.
Black silk hood lined with russet-brown silk denotes M.A. of London.
Black silk hood lined with dark blue silk denotes M. A. of Dublin or
Queens. (Irel.).
Black silk hood lined with red-purple silk (colour of bell heather—Erica
Tetralix) denotes M.A. of Glasgow.

MISSIONS
ABORIGINAL CHILDREN’S INDUSTRIAL HOME, dio. of Perth,
is part of the work undertaken by the Missions Committee near Carnarvon,
in the district of Gascoyne, where there are Mission buildings and land.
CHINESE MIS., dio. of Brisb,, is carried on by Mr. King Tim, a
Catechist, who receives a salary of £l3O a year.
CHINESE MIS., dio. of Syd. Rev. George Soo Hoo Ten is the
Missionary, and a Chinese Catechist assists in the work. A Church for
Chinese has been erected at Botany, and services are held in School-
houses at several Chinese centres.
CHURCH HOME, dio. of Syd., founded 1885 to help fallen women.
The payments for work done by the inmates and free contributions provide
for the expenses of the Home,
CHURCH MISSIONARY SOCIETY OF VICTORIA, dio. of Melb.
CHURCH MIS, to the Aborigines, dio. of Melb.
INSTITUTION FOR HALF-CASTE CHILDREN, dio. of Perth, is
now established at Swan.
KANAKA MIS., dio. of Brisb., Classes are held at Maryborough and
Bundaberg. J 6
MELANESIAN MIS., dio. of Brisb., a class is held in Brisbane.
MELANESIAN MIS., includes the Solomon Islands and the islands
South to the Headquarters and Schools at Norfolk Island. Missionary
work was first undertaken in 1848. The staff consists of seven British and
six Native clergy, and 145 teachers. There are 72 Mission schools and
stations in the Islands, with 2514 native scholars. Income from Endow-
ment about £1,500, and from voluntary sources about £5,000.
134
THE AUSTRALIAN ANGLICAN


MIS. TO SEAMEN, dio. of Syd., was created as a voluntary work
by the then Missionary, who in 1881 became a salaried agent. The
Mission undertakes a varied work on ship-board, at the Shipping Office,
Hospitals, Gaols, and at Trafalgar House, where a reading-room and other
attractions are provided for sailors.
NEW GUINEA MIS. Established by and under the direction of the
Aust. Board of Mis. £3OOO a year is the estimated expense of working
the Mis. The Revs. A. A. M'Laren and Copland King, with two lay-
teachers are the present staff. The Mis. has charge of all the East Coast
of the British territory. The headquarters will be at Chad’s Bay.
POONINDIE NATIVE INSTITUTION, dio. of Adel., founded
1850 by Archd. (afternoon Bishop) Hale, to Christianise aboriginals. First
located at Boston Is and, removed to Port Lincoln. The Bp. and two
other Trustees have 15,000 acres of land for the Mission at a peppercorn
rental, and three sections of freehold land. The stock consists of about
8,000 sheep, 46 cattle, 24 horses, and 12 pigs. 105 bales of wool, 400 bags
of wheat and 25 bags of barley is about the produce of a year. The Mission
is self supporting. The baker and horse feeder are the only two white
men employed.

Church Sunday School Magazine, published ac Bowral, dio. of Syd.

SUNDAY SCHOOLS.—Sunday School Association, dio. of Melb.
SUNDAY SCHOOL INSTITUTE, dio. of Goulburn, has for its
objects (a) the erection of separate buildings for S.S. use; (b) improving
management and method of S.S. ; ( c) helping teachers by model lessons,
lectures, and addresses, selecting lessons, and holding voluntary examina-
tions of teachers. The Institute consists of the clergy, superintendents of
Sunday Schools, teachers other than probationers, and subscribers of £1 a
year.
SUNDAY SCHOOL INSTITUTE, dio. of Sydney (Rev. E. C.
Beck, Sec.), established 1882, circulates information as to best methods of
organising and conducting S.S. Branch Associations in the several Rural
Deaneries, arrange for special services, conferences of teachers, etc. The
Institute provides churchmen to give addresses, training lessons, and model
lessons to teachers.
SUNDAY SCHOOL UNION, dio. of Adelaide, consists of 36 Schools
in Union. The objects are (1) mutual co-operation, (2) formation and
improvement of schools, (3) fellowship of teachers, (4) stimulation and
encouragement, (5) diffusion of improved appliances and methods, (6)
efficient religious education, (7) provision of code of lessons, (8) provision
of literature and entertainments, (9) transact Adelaide business for country
schools, (10) examination of teachers. Schools supply annual statistics and
subscribe from 20s. to ss. according to number of scholars. Teachers sub-
scribe 2s. 6d., honorary members £1 Is. a year, and life members a donation
of £5 ss.

The School was formerly opened in May, 1889 by His Excellency
the Governor.
The buildings consist of the School House, containiog accommodation
for about thirty boarders, who are under the care of Miss Robson and an
experienced Matron ; of a Dining Hall, capable of accommodating over one
hundred boys ; and a block of eight large Class Rooms.
The Grounds (of about four acres) offer exceptional facilities for
athletic gsmes, and,' in addition,'a Boat Club has been formed.
The School aims at giving a thorough training to boys preparing for
the University and the learned professions, as well as to such as are intended
for commercial or country life.
